# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka SASL Mechanism Configuration Validation

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that validate SASL mechanism configuration at broker startup: the sasl.enabled.mechanisms validation, the JAAS config presence check, and the mechanism-specific configuration validation (SCRAM, GSSAPI, OAUTHBEARER).

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

62-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed my analysis of the Kafka broker's SASL mechanism configuration validation. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I've identified **10 Java source files** in apache/kafka that validate SASL mechanism configuration at broker startup, organized into three main validation categories:

### 1. **sasl.enabled.mechanisms Validation**
- **BrokerSecurityConfigs.java**: Defines the SASL_ENABLED_MECHANISMS_CONFIG property
- **KafkaConfig.scala**: Validates that the inter-broker SASL mechanism is included in enabled mechanisms (lines 627-629)

### 2. **JAAS Config Presence Check**
- **JaasContext.java**: Validates that JAAS configuration exists and contains exactly one login module (lines 92-101). When no dynamic config is provided, it validates the context exists in the JAAS file (lines 145-150).
- **ChannelBuilders.java**: Loads JaasContext for each enabled mechanism during broker startup (lines 137-140)

### 3. **Mechanism-Specific Configuration Validation**
- **PLAIN**: PlainServerCallbackHandler.java - stores and validates user credentials from JAAS
- **SCRAM**: ScramServerCallbackHandler.java - initializes credential cache for SCRAM-SHA-256/512
- **GSSAPI**: SaslChannelBuilder.java - creates KerberosShortNamer for principal mapping and validates Kerberos configuration
- **OAUTHBEARER**: OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler.java and BrokerJwtValidator.java - validate JWT configuration and initialization

The validation chain executes during broker startup when listeners are configured, ensuring all enabled SASL mechanisms have proper JAAS configuration and mechanism-specific settings before the broker accepts client connections.

The complete findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

This allows for &quot;live&quot; private key rotation without restarting the Kafka client.</p>\\\"\\n281:         + ASSERTION_FILE_MUTUAL_EXCLUSION_NOTICE;\\n282: \\n283:     public static final String SASL_OAUTHBEARER_ASSERTION_PRIVATE_KEY_PASSPHRASE = \\\"sasl.oauthbearer.assertion.private.key.passphrase\\\";\\n284:     public static final String SASL_OAUTHBEARER_ASSERTION_PRIVATE_KEY_PASSPHRASE_DOC = \\\"<p>The optional passphrase to decrypt the private key file specified by\\\"\\n285:         + \\\" <code>sasl.oauthbearer.assertion.private.key.file</code>.</p>\\\"\\n286:         + \\\"<p><em>Note</em>: If the file referred to by <code>sasl.oauthbearer.assertion.private.key.file</code> is modified on the file system at runtime and it was\\\"\\n287:         + \\\" created with a <em>different</em> passphrase than it was previously, the client will not be able to access the private key file because the passphrase is now\\\"\\n288:         + \\\" out of date.
